ChatGPT:

Ja, det er præcis det afsnit jeg mener.

Problemet er, at første sætning siger:

```text
averaged over 9 active seeds, excluding the collapsed seed 6
```

men dine figurer/plot captions kan samtidig være baseret på **alle 10 seeds**, hvor seed 6 bidrager med 0%. Det kan skabe uklarhed.

Jeg ville rette afsnittet til denne version:

```markdown
### 6.1 Eval return and Sharpe curves

The eval return learning curve should be interpreted as a diagnostic curve rather than as a
formal convergence proof. In the all-seed plot, the mean is computed across all 10 seeds,
with the collapsed seed 6 contributing 0% return. This makes the figure conservative and
keeps the full multiseed outcome visible.

The curve rises during early and mid training, reaches its highest level around training
step 10,000, and then declines toward step 25,000. This pattern suggests that, for this
configuration, earlier stopping may have produced higher mean eval return. This should be
treated as an early-stopping hypothesis only, not as a final conclusion. No formal
validation-based early-stopping criterion was used in this experiment.

The Sharpe ratio shows a broadly similar pattern, improving during early and mid training
before plateauing or slightly declining later. Because Sharpe is undefined for the fully
collapsed seed 6, Sharpe-based summaries should be interpreted with care and should be read
alongside the return, trade-count, and HOLD-diagnostic plots.

The standard deviation across seeds remains large throughout training, reflecting genuine
inter-seed variance in learned policies rather than a single stable convergence pattern.
```

Det er mere robust, fordi det siger:

```text
- return plot: all 10 seeds, seed 6 = 0%
- Sharpe: seed 6 kan være undefined/null
- early stopping = hypothesis, ikke conclusion
- ikke klassisk konvergens
```

Hvis du vil have en kortere version til LaTeX, kan du bruge:

```latex
\subsubsection{Eval return and Sharpe curves}

The eval return learning curve is interpreted as a diagnostic curve rather than as formal
convergence evidence. In the all-seed plot, the mean is computed across all 10 seeds, with
the collapsed seed 6 contributing 0\% return. The curve rises during early and mid training,
reaches its highest level around training step 10{,}000, and then declines toward step
25{,}000. This suggests that earlier stopping may have produced higher mean eval return for
this configuration, but this should be treated as a hypothesis only, since no formal
validation-based early-stopping criterion was used.

The Sharpe curve follows a broadly similar pattern, although Sharpe is undefined for the
fully collapsed seed 6 and should therefore be interpreted with care. Both curves exhibit
substantial inter-seed variance, supporting the interpretation that the clean IQN baseline
learns non-trivial but seed-sensitive policies rather than a single stable convergence
trajectory.
```

```markdown
**Figure [X]:** *Eval total return over training steps for `clean_25k_baseline_v1`
(mean ± 1 std across all 10 seeds, with seed 6 contributing 0% return). Peak performance
occurs around step 10,000, after which mean eval return declines. This suggests a possible
early-stopping effect, but no formal early-stopping criterion was used.*
```

## Find dette i `.tex`

```latex
The mean eval return (averaged over the 9 active seeds) rises from approximately 32\% at
training step 0 to a peak of approximately 83\% at step 10{,}000, then declines to
approximately 55\% at step 25{,}000. The standard deviation is large throughout, reflecting
genuine inter-seed policy variance.

The observed eval curve suggests that, for this configuration, \textbf{earlier stopping may
have produced higher mean eval return}. This should be treated as an early-stopping
hypothesis only. No formal early-stopping criterion was applied. Validation-based early
stopping and eval-Sharpe plateau detection are identified as future work.

The IQN training loss grows monotonically from approximately 6 at step 2{,}000 to
approximately 50 at step 25{,}000. \textbf{This is not evidence of divergence} -- Q-value
spread remains stable throughout training -- but it indicates that training targets are not
stabilising within the 25{,}000-step horizon. The thesis does not claim that the IQN loss
converges in the classical supervised-learning sense. Policy quality is assessed from eval
return and Sharpe metrics.
```

## Erstat med dette

```latex
The eval return learning curve is interpreted as a diagnostic curve rather than as formal
convergence evidence. In the all-seed plot, the mean is computed across all 10 seeds, with
the collapsed seed 6 contributing 0\% return. The curve rises during early and mid training,
reaches its highest level around training step 10{,}000, and then declines toward step
25{,}000. This suggests that earlier stopping may have produced higher mean eval return for
this configuration, but this should be treated as a hypothesis only, since no formal
validation-based early-stopping criterion was used.

fully collapsed seed 6 and should therefore be interpreted with care. Both curves exhibit
substantial inter-seed variance, supporting the interpretation that the clean IQN baseline
learns non-trivial but seed-sensitive policies rather than a single stable convergence
trajectory.

The IQN training loss grows monotonically from approximately 6 at step 2{,}000 to
approximately 50 at step 25{,}000. \textbf{This is not evidence of divergence} -- Q-value
spread remains stable throughout training -- but it indicates that training targets are not
stabilising within the 25{,}000-step horizon. The thesis does not claim that the IQN loss
converges in the classical supervised-learning sense. Policy quality is assessed from eval
return, Sharpe, trade-count, and HOLD-diagnostic metrics.
```

## V1 — hvad findes der?

V1 er en mindre og mere direkte kodebase under:

```text

```

Den består især af:

```text

data/
envs/
rl/
runner/
```

### 1. Algorithmic trading baselines

V1 har en ret stærk samling af klassiske/non-RL tradingstrategier:

```text

ema_crossover
momentum

rsi_mean_reversion
macd_signal
volatility_filter
equal_weight_buy_and_hold_portfolio
```

Det er stærkt, fordi problemformuleringen lægger op til at sammenligne RL/distributional RL med mere klassiske beslutningsmodeller. V1 giver dig et mere intuitivt “hvad gør en regelbaseret strategi?”-grundlag.

### 2. PIT split utility

V1 har:

```text
src/stockdss/data/point_in_time_split.py
```

Den laver train/trade split fra én master market data file og gemmer metadata. Det er direkte relevant, fordi problemformuleringen kræver historisk backtesting uden look-ahead bias. 

### 3. Minimal discrete FinRL-style environment

V1 har:

```text

```

med simple actions:

```text

SELL_100
```

Det er stærkt som didaktisk bridge fra CartPole/IQN til aktiehandel. Det er lettere at forklare end V2’s mere komplekse DSS action resolver.

### 4. Core IQN implementation

V1 har:

```text

src/stockdss/rl/nets/iqn_net.py

src/stockdss/rl/config/iqn_config.py
```

Det er en renere og mere pædagogisk IQN-kerne:

```text

online + target networks
replay buffer
tau sampling
quantile Huber loss
Double-DQN-style target selection
```

Den er god til thesis-forklaring, fordi den er mindre pakket ind i run-logik.

### 5. V1 decision-distribution visualizer

Dette er måske det mest interessante ift. dit nuværende roadmap:

```text

```

Den laver præcis de typer figurer, der matcher “decision support”:

```text

approximate return distribution per action
risk-adjusted action score

risk-adjusted score = q50 - λ * |CVaR10|
```

Det er meget stærkt jfr. problemformuleringen, fordi det visualiserer **hvorfor** en handling anbefales, ikke kun hvilken handling modellen vælger.

### 6. Summary runner

Den samler:

Det er stærkt som “thesis table/figure generator”, fordi den kombinerer flere kilder i ét overblik.

## Hvad er stærkt i V1 jfr. problemformuleringen?

V1’s styrke er ikke robust reproducibility. V1’s styrke er **formidling og decision-support-forklaring**.

Det stærkeste i V1 er:

```text
1. IQN quantile visualisering per action
2. return distribution per action
3. risk-adjusted score med CVaR
4. simple BUY/HOLD/SELL-style action semantics
5. klassiske algorithmic trading baselines
6. overskuelig summary dashboard
```

I forhold til problemformuleringen rammer V1 især disse ting:

```text
risk-sensitive sequential decisions
buy/hold/sell decision support
return distributions rather than only expected return
investor-facing explanation of uncertainty/risk
baseline comparison against non-RL strategies
```

Det V1 ikke er stærkest til:

```text
manifest-driven reproducibility
strict Mode A/Mode B separation
robust run registry
multiseed evidence
config verification
HDP/EDL integration
point-in-time fundamentals
clean thesis evidence package
```

Så V1 skal ikke være den nye hovedpipeline. V1 skal bruges som **visualization/design inspiration**.

## Min vigtigste konklusion

Du skal **ikke** tilbage til V1 som pipeline.

Du skal bruge V1 som:

```text
visualization and explanation donor
```

og V2 som:

```text
canonical thesis experiment pipeline
```

Altså:

```text

V2 → rigtige data, rigtige runs, rigtige artifacts, rigtige thesis evidence
```

## Hvad betyder det for “V1 thesis visualization ports”?

Det punkt giver nu meget mere mening.

Du bør ikke bare lave flere generiske plots. Du bør specifikt porte de V1-visuals, som V2 mangler:

```text
1. IQN quantile function per action
2. Estimated return distribution per action
3. Risk-adjusted score per action
4. Decision table with q10/q25/q50/q75/q90/CVaR
5. Risk-neutral vs risk-adjusted selected action
6. Investor-facing “why this action?” dashboard
```

Det passer langt bedre til problemformuleringen end kun learning curves, fordi decision support handler om at gøre anbefalinger forståelige og risikobevidste.

## Min anbefalede næste retning

Før vi beder Copilot implementere noget, vil jeg foreslå at vi definerer denne overgang:

```text
V1 thesis visualization ports ⬅️ NOW
  - port IQN quantile function per action from V1 to V2 artifacts
  - port return distribution per action from V1 to V2 artifacts
  - port risk-adjusted score-per-action plot from V1 to V2 artifacts
  - port decision-support dashboard concept from V1 to V2 artifacts
  - use clean 25k eval_distributions.csv as real source
  - do not use V1 demo values except as fallback/example
  - output thesis-ready figures under outputs/run_registry/...
```

Det næste rigtige step er derfor en **plan**, ikke implementering:

```text
Find exactly which V2 files contain q10/q25/q50/q75/q90/CVaR per action
Map those columns into V1-style plot functions
Create a V2-native runner that outputs thesis-ready IQN decision-distribution plots
```

Det er den rigtige måde at bruge V1 på.

"
Data-Driven Stock Investment Decision Support
A Reinforcement Learning Approach to Risk-Sensitive Sequential Portfolio Decisions
Project Contract / Master Thesis Proposal
Jannik Busse Guldmand
MSc Data Science (ICT Systems), SDU
jagul24@student.sdu.dk
Supervisor: Professor Melih Kandemir
Contents
Problem
This thesis addresses data-driven decision support for stock investors operating under uncertainty.
Investors continuously face sequential decisions regarding which stocks to buy, hold, or sell, how
to adjust portfolio risk exposure, and when changes in market conditions may justify a shift in
investment strategy. In practice, these decisions are guided by an investor’s overarching strategy,
risk profile, and focus areas, but their implementation is often inconsistent and insufficient in
handling market uncertainty and the continuous arrival of new information.
The goal of this thesis is to develop a data-driven, near real-time decision support system for
stock investment that assists investors in translating a chosen strategy into consistent, risk-aware
decisions. The objective is not to construct a system designed to systematically beat the market,
but to improve investor outcomes relative to intuition-based or ad hoc decision making, by
supporting decisions that are grounded in data, models, and explicit risk considerations.
The system operates within the framework defined by the investor’s strategy and risk profile,
but supports different starting scenarios. If the investor already holds an existing portfolio or
predefined list of stocks, recommendations are anchored in this starting point. Alternatively, if
the investor specifies only an investment horizon, risk profile, and possible thematic preferences,
the system can also propose stocks as part of portfolio construction.
The system generates buy/hold/sell recommendations for portfolio positions and indicates when
adjustments to portfolio exposure or investment strategy may be appropriate in response to new
information or changing market conditions. The system is not an autonomous trading algorithm,
but a data-driven decision support tool.
Data
The primary data framework for this project is FinRL, which provides historical market data
and an environment structure suitable for reinforcement learning in financial decision-making
tasks. FinRL serves as the foundation for price-based and market-related information used in
the experiments.
In addition to the standard market data available in FinRL, the state representation will be
extended with additional structured information sources obtained via APIs. These sources may
1
include financial key figures, accounting-based indicators, company announcements, press releases,
stock market news, macroeconomic indicators, and potentially other quantified information
relevant to stock investment decisions.
These information sources are incorporated as quantified features in the observation state. The
purpose is to reflect how real-world investors rely on multiple information channels when making
decisions, while maintaining a consistent data-driven modeling framework.
For evaluation, historical backtesting will follow a point-in-time setup, ensuring that at each
decision point only information that would have been available at that time is used. This prevents
look-ahead bias and ensures a realistic simulation of near real-time decision support.
Methodology
The methodological foundation of this thesis is reinforcement learning (RL) for sequential decision-
making in financial environments. The decision support system is modeled as a sequential portfolio
decision problem, where the agent learns policies for buy/hold/sell actions under uncertainty.
The study compares different approaches to value representation in RL. A baseline is provided
by parametric RL methods, where value functions represent expected future returns. In contrast,
the thesis investigates distributional reinforcement learning, where the return is modeled as a
full probability distribution rather than a single expectation. In particular, Implicit Quantile
Networks (IQN)[1] are considered as a framework for learning return distributions in a flexible
and continuous manner.
Furthermore, the thesis explores uncertainty-aware modeling by incorporating an epistemic
uncertainty component inspired by Evidential Deep Learning[2]. This allows the system to
account not only for stochastic return variability but also for uncertainty in the model’s own
estimates, which is particularly relevant in financial environments characterized by limited data
and regime shifts.
Within this framework, decision policies are optimized with respect to risk-sensitive objectives
derived from the learned return distributions, enabling analysis of how uncertainty modeling
influences portfolio decisions, stability, and risk handling.
Evaluation
The system is designed as a near real-time stock investment decision support framework, where
recommendations are continuously updated as new market and information signals arrive.
In the evaluation, this real-time behavior is simulated through historical walk-forward backtesting
using a point-in-time setup to avoid look-ahead bias. At each decision step, only information
that would have been available at that historical time is used, ensuring a realistic assessment of
data-driven decision support under evolving market conditions.
The primary success criterion is to maximize portfolio returns within the investor’s given strategy
and risk profile, while maintaining consistent handling of downside risk.
Performance will be assessed using:
• cumulative returns
• risk-adjusted performance measures (e.g., Sharpe ratio)
• maximum drawdown
• selected downside risk measures
2
Comparisons will be made between parametric RL agents (modeling expected returns) and
distributional or uncertainty-aware RL agents (modeling return distributions), in order to
investigate how different value representations influence risk exposure, decision stability, and
performance across varying market regimes.
Distribution of work
The following is an approximate distribution of workload for the thesis:
• Literature review and theoretical foundations (RL, distributional RL, uncertainty modeling):
20%
• Data integration, environment setup, and feature construction (FinRL and additional data
sources): 20%
• Implementation of reinforcement learning models and uncertainty-aware methods: 30%
• Experimental evaluation, backtesting, and hypothesis testing: 20%
• Thesis writing and documentation: 10%

Bibliography
[1] Will Dabney et al. “Implicit Quantile Networks for Distributional Reinforcement
Learning”. In: Proceedings of the 35th International Conference on Machine Learning
(ICML) (2018). arXiv: 1806.06923. URL: https://arxiv.org/abs/1806.06923.
[2] Murat Sensoy, Lance Kaplan, and Melih Kandemir. “Evidential Deep Learning to
Quantify Classification Uncertainty”. In: Advances in Neural Information Processing
Systems (NeurIPS) (2018). URL: https://papers.nips.cc/paper_files/paper/
2018/hash/a981f2b708044d6fb4a71a1463242520-Abstract.html
"

## Det stærkeste i Copilots vurdering

Copilot identificerer V1’s centrale fil som:

```text
external/ObjectRL_style/src/stockdss/rl/experiments/visualize_iqn_decision_distribution.py
```

og anbefaler at portere idéerne:

```text
1. IQN quantile function per action
2. Approximate return distribution per action
3. Risk-adjusted score per action
4. q10/q25/q50/q75/q90/CVaR/score decision table
5. Combined 4-panel IQN decision dashboard
```

Det er præcis det, V2 mangler lige nu: V2 har clean diagnostic plots, men de er mest **debug/evaluation plots**. De viser seed-level behavior, HOLD collapse, loss, epsilon og learning curves. De forklarer ikke endnu særlig godt:

```text
“Why did the DSS recommend this action?”
```

V1’s dashboard gør netop dét.

## Det jeg ville rette/nuancere i Copilots vurdering

Der er én ting, jeg ville være lidt forsigtig med:

Copilot skriver, at seed 5 bør bruges som “representative seed” og at `train_step=10000` eller `25000` kan bruges. Jeg er enig i retningen, men jeg ville ikke kun lave én snapshot. Jeg ville lave **to snapshot modes**:

```text
A) final policy snapshot: seed 5, train_step=25000
B) peak checkpoint snapshot: seed 5, train_step=10000
```

Hvorfor?

Fordi clean 25k evidence allerede viser, at eval return topper omkring 10k og falder mod 25k. Hvis du kun viser 25k, viser du final policy. Hvis du også viser 10k, kan du forklare early-stopping-hypotesen bedre.

Jeg ville også overveje:

```text
C) contrast snapshot: seed 6, train_step=25000
```

Det viser, hvordan en HOLD-collapse distribution ser ud.

Så min port-prioritet er:

```text
1. seed 5 @ 25000 — final active policy
2. seed 5 @ 10000 — peak/early-stopping diagnostic
3. seed 6 @ 25000 — collapsed policy contrast
```
